Refining Non-Evident Concomitance: Sensory and Empirical Evidence
Author broadens the definition of non-evident to include intuitions and sensory evidence beyond the middle term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which types of knowledge (sensory, empirical, intuitive) are included under non-evident concomitance and explain why the definition was broadened.

Core Idea
Non-evident concomitance includes not only syllogistic proof but also direct sensory or empirical certainty.

In classical logic, 'non-evident' (ghayr bayyin) commonly meant a concomitance that required a middle term for certainty. However, the commentator (al-muḥashshī) observed that some certainties—like feeling fire's heat or seeing the world's change—do not need a syllogism yet are not self-evident from the concepts alone. This lesson explores why the definition was broadened and how to recognize these cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the standard definition of non-evident
Find the famous interpretation of non-evident (ghayr bayyin) that the author mentions. What does it require for certainty?
The standard view says it needs an intermediary (wāsiṭa), typically a middle term in a syllogism.
2
Locate the problem with that definition
The author argues that some certainties (e.g., sensory, empirical) do not need a middle term but are not self-evident either. What would happen if we kept the narrow definition?
They would be misclassified as self-evident or not properly accounted for.
3
Understand the examples given
The passage lists intuitive (ḥadsī), empirical (tajribī), and sensory (ḥissī) knowledge. Think of an example from Islamic sciences: e.g., the heat of fire from touch is sensory, and it gives certainty without a syllogism.
These are immediate but not conceptual—they require external evidence.
4
Extract the broadened definition
How does the commentator (al-muḥashshī) redefine non-evident? It is that which does not produce certainty from mere conception of terms and relation, but needs either a middle term (if theoretical) or something else (if immediate but not conceptual).
The new definition includes both syllogistic and experiential evidence.
5
Apply to a new Islamic example
Consider the Qur'anic statement: 'Indeed, with hardship comes ease' (94:6). Is the concomitance of ease after hardship self-evident or non-evident? Which type of evidence provides certainty?
It is non-evident because it is not logically necessary from the concepts alone; it is known through revelation (an external source).

Source Text

His saying: (And at that point, the non-evident is the necessary concomitant that... he only deviated from his famous interpretation among the people, which is that it needs an intermediary for the mind to be certain of the concomitance between them, because of what follows from that: that there exists a division of the non-necessary [actually non-evident?] falling under one of the two divisions. And that is because the intermediary, according to their interpretation, is what accompanies our saying 'because' when one says 'because it is such'. For example, when we say 'the world is originated because it is changing', 'the changing' is the middle term because it is the one accompanying our saying 'because' when we said 'because it is changing'. And it is apparent that it does not follow from the absence of the need for an intermediary for the concomitance that from the conception of the concomitant together with the conception of the subject and the relation between them, the certainty of the concomitance follows, because it is possible that there exists a necessary concomitant that does not need an intermediary and yet does not necessitate certainty from the conception of both and the relation, such as intuitive, empirical, and sensory matters. Therefore the commentator broadened his interpretation and said: it is the necessary concomitant whose conception together with the conception of the subject and the relation between them does not necessitate certainty of concomitance, but rather needs an intermediary or something else from intuition, experience, sense, or something else. (Muhammad ‘Ali) (140) i.e., rather it needs an intermediary in the mentioned sense if it is theoretical, or something else besides the conception of the two terms and the relation if it is self-evident but different from the first type, like intuitive, empirical, or sensory. So the self-evident different from the first type is included in the non-evident concomitance, as is understood from the commentator's speech at the end of the commentary, and from the later ones...
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage refines the definition of non-evident (ghayr bayyin) concomitance. The famous interpretation required an intermediary (wāsita), typically a middle term (hadd awsaṭ) in a syllogism, like 'changing' in 'the world is originated because it is changing'. However, the author argues that there are cases where no syllogistic middle term is needed, yet the concomitance is not automatically certain from the terms alone. Examples include intuitive (hadsī), empirical (tajribī), and sensory (hissī) certainties. For instance, the heat of fire when sensed directly gives certainty without a syllogism. Therefore, the commentator (al-muḥashshī) broadened the definition: non-evident concomitance is that which does not produce certainty from the mere conception of the subject, concomitant, and relation, but requires either a middle term (if theoretical) or something else like intuition, experience, or sense perception if the evidence is immediate but not simply from the concepts. In sum, non-evident includes both what needs proof and what needs direct experience.

Key Terms
الواسطة (al-wāsiṭa): A middle term in a syllogism that is needed to establish certainty of concomitance in theoretical matters.
الحدسي (al-ḥadsī): Intuitive knowledge that does not require a syllogistic middle term but is immediate.
التجريبي (al-tajribī): Empirical knowledge based on repeated experience, providing certainty without a formal syllogism.
الحسي (al-ḥissī): Sensory knowledge, immediate through sense perception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To include cases where the middle term is unknown.
B) To include cases where certainty comes from sense perception or experience without a syllogism.
C) To exclude self-evident propositions.
D) To create more divisions of the necessary concomitant.

Key Takeaway
The definition of non-evident concomitance must include cases where certainty comes from sense, experience, or intuition, not only from a syllogistic middle term.

Necessary Parts of a Definition: The Five Universals
Author discusses which five universals are necessary parts of a definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which of the five universals are considered necessary components of a definition according to later logicians, and explain the critique of the standard definition of 'mu'arif'.

Core Idea
Not all five universals are needed; later logicians restrict definitions to genus and differentia (hadd) or property and accident (rasm).

This passage from the Hashiya clarifies a key point in the theory of definition: which of the five universals are actually required to compose a proper definition. It also refines the very concept of 'definiens' (mu'arif) by critiquing a common formulation and offering a more precise understanding through the lens of systematic consideration (nazar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the five universals mentioned
List the five predicables: genus, species, differentia, property, and general accident. Note that the passage states that later logicians (including the author) exclude species and general accident from definitions.
Species is excluded because it is the definiendum itself; general accident is too broad to be distinctive.
2
Understand the exclusion of species and general accident
The passage says that definitions (hadd and rasm) do not include species or general accident. Species is not used because it would be circular (the definiendum is a species). General accident is not used because it does not specify the essence.
The exclusion is a shift from earlier logic where all five were considered.
3
Analyze the critique of the definition of 'mu'arif'
The standard definition says the definiens entails conception of the definiendum. The commentator points out two problems: (1) evident concomitants (e.g., smoke entails fire, but smoke is not a definition) and (2) the reflexivity problem: the definiens itself presupposes conception of the definiendum.
This critique refines the understanding of what a definition should achieve.
4
Examine al-Muhaqqiq al-Sharif's response
Al-Sharif argues that the entailment is not absolute but 'by way of consideration' (nazar). The purpose of logic is to provide a method for acquiring conceptions and assents, so the definiens is only a tool that leads to conception when properly considered.
This preserves the utility of definitions while avoiding the logical pitfalls.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المراد مما يتركب منه المعرف ليس الكليات الخمس يجميعها فان العرض العام غير معتبر في التعريفات عند المتأخرين منهم المصنف و سيصرح بذلك و كذا النوع على ما يفهم من اطلاقاتهم حيث انهم حضروا المعرف على الحد والرسم ولم يعتبروا في واحد منهما النوع والعرض العام ايضاً بل انما ذكرا فيما تقدم للاستطراد و استقصاء لاقسام الكليات. قال بعض المحققين من المحشين و يمكن ان يقال: ان مراد المحشى (ره) منه الكليات الخمس يجميعها لان النوع يجوز ان يكون جزء للمعرف كتعريف الرومى بانه انسان كذا والعرض العام ايضاً يجوز ان يكون جزء للمعرف كما سيجيء انشاء الله تعالى. و اقول: هذا و ان كان حقاً في نفسه، لكنه لا يلائم بنسبة الفراغ الى المصنف فتأمل. (میرزا محمد علی) (۲) قوله ليفيد تصور هذا الشيء: هذا القيد لاخراج المحمول الذى لم يكن الغرض منه القادة التصور ثم انه عدل عن التعريف المشهور و هو يستلزم تصوره تصور هذا الشيء، لانتقاضه بالملزومات بالنسبة الى لوازمها البيئة و بالمعرف من حيث هو معرف فان تصوره من حيث هو كذلك اى المعرف يستلزم تصور معرفه لان تحقق تصوره من هذه الحيثية لا يكون الأبعد تصور معرفه، فظهر من ذلك ضعف ما يقال من ان استلزام تصور المعرف بالكسر ممنوع بان تصور الشيء مجملاً لا يستلزم تصوره مفصلاً. الضعف ان تصور المعرف مجملاً لا يكون الا بعد تصور معرفه مفصلاً فقد استلزم تصور المعرف و وجه من حيث انه كذلك تصور المعرف استلزام المعلول للملة وظهر ايضاً ضعف ما اورده المحقق الدواني من ان تصور ماهية المعرف قد يحصل بدون المعرف بالوجه السابق على الكسب. و اجاب المحقق الشريف عن الانتقاض : بان المراد من الاستلزام بطريق النظر بقرينة ما سبق من ان الموصل بالنظر الى التصور يسمى قولاً شارحاً وان المقصود من الفن بيان طريق اكتساب التصورات و التصديقات. (عبد الرحيم)
What is meant by the components of the definiens is not all five universals, for general accident is not considered in definitions according to the later scholars, including the author, and he will explicitly state that, and likewise species as understood from their usages, since they restricted the definiens to definition and description and did not consider in either of them species and general accident. Rather they only mentioned them previously for digression and to exhaust the divisions of the universals. One of the verifying scholars among the glossators said: It can be said that the glossator (may God have mercy on him) meant by it the five universals all together, because species can be a part of the definiens, as in the definition of the Roman as 'a human being such-and-such,' and likewise general accident can be a part of the definiens, as will come in the future, God willing. I say: This, although true in itself, does not agree with attributing negligence to the author, so reflect. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (2) His statement: 'to inform of the conception of this thing': this restriction is to exclude the predicate whose purpose is not the benefit of conception. Then he changed from the famous definition, which is 'it entails its conception of this thing,' because it is refuted by the implications with respect to their evident concomitants, and by the definiens inasmuch as it is a definiens—for its conception in that respect, i.e. the definiens, entails the conception of the definiendum, because the actualization of its conception in this respect does not occur except after the conception of the definiendum. Thus appears the weakness of what is said that the entailment of the conception of the definiens (kasr) is denied because the conception of a thing in summary does not entail its conception in detail. The weakness is that the conception of the definiens in summary occurs only after the conception of the definiendum in detail; thus the conception of the definiens in that respect entails the conception of the definiendum, as the effect entails the cause. And also appears the weakness of what al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawwani objected, that the conception of the essence of the definiendum may occur without the definiens in the manner preceding acquisition. And al-Muhaqqiq al-Sharif responded to the refutation: that what is meant by entailment is by way of consideration, as indicated by what preceded, that that which leads by consideration to conception is called an explanatory statement, and the purpose of the art is to explain the way of acquiring conceptions and assents. (Abd al-Rahim)
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the composition of the definiens (mu'arif). It begins by clarifying that not all five universals are required parts of a definition; later logicians, including the author, exclude species (naw') and general accident ('arad 'amm). The discussion then shifts to a refinement of the definition of 'mu'arif' itself, critiquing the well-known definition that says the definiens entails conception of the definiendum. The commentator points out problems with that definition, such as cases of evident concomitants and the reflexive nature of the definiens. A response by al-Muhaqqiq al-Sharif is given, arguing that the entailment is by way of systematic consideration (nazar), consistent with the purpose of logic as a tool for acquiring conceptions and assents.

Key Terms
معرف (بكسر الراء)
حد
رسم
الكليات الخمس
عرض عام

Key Takeaway
Later logicians exclude species and general accident from definitions, and the standard definition of 'mu'arif' is refined to mean 'that which leads by systematic consideration to conception of the definiendum.'

Which Universals Belong in a Definition?
Author critiques the view that all five universals are used in definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which universals are excluded from definitions according to later logicians and explain the debate over their inclusion in the definiens.

Core Idea
Not all five universals belong in every definition — species and general accident are often excluded.

In classical Mantiq, definitions are built from universals. But which universals actually appear in a definition? This passage reveals a key refinement: later logicians, including the author of our text, exclude species and general accident from the definiens. A commentator objects with examples where they seem necessary. Your task is to follow this critical exchange and understand the final position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim being refined
Read the first part: the author states that the five universals are not all used in definitions. Find the exact words that exclude 'arad 'amm and naw'.
The key phrase is 'العرض العام غير معتبر في التعريفات عند المتأخرين'.
2
Locate the grounds for exclusion
The author says that definitions are restricted to hadd and rasm, and neither includes species or general accident. They were only mentioned earlier for completeness (istitrad). Why might species be excluded? Because species is already the definiendum in many cases?
Think about the role of species as a part of the definition of a subspecies, but not for a universal definition of the species itself.
3
Understand the commentator's objection
A commentator (ba'd al-muhaqqiqin) argues that species can be part of the definiens, e.g., defining 'Rumi human' as 'such an animal'. General accident can also appear, as will be shown later. What is the force of this objection?
The objection is that exclusion is too strong; there are legitimate cases.
4
Assess the author's final position
The author concedes the truth of the objection but says it does not fit the original author's intention. This is a typical move in hashia: acknowledging a point but maintaining the original context. What does this tell you about the limits of the original claim?
The original claim may refer to the most common definitions, not all possible ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱) المراد مما يتركب منه المعرف ليس الكليات الخمس يجميعها فان العرض العام غير معتبر في التعريفات عند المتأخرين منهم المصنف و سيصرح بذلك و كذا النوع على ما يفهم من اطلاقاتهم حيث انهم حضروا المعرف على الحد والرسم ولم يعتبروا في واحد منهما النوع والعرض العام ايضاً بل انما ذكرا فيما تقدم للاستطراد و استقصاء لاقسام الكليات. قال بعض المحققين من المحشين و يمكن ان يقال: ان مراد المحشى (ره) منه الكليات الخمس يجميعها لان النوع يجوز ان يكون جزء للمعرف كتعريف الرومى بانه انسان كذا والعرض العام ايضاً يجوز ان يكون جزء للمعرف كما سيجيء انشاء الله تعالى. و اقول: هذا و ان كان حقاً في نفسه، لكنه لا يلائم بنسبة الفراغ الى المصنف فتأمل. (میرزا محمد علی)
(1) What is meant by the components of the definiens is not all five universals collectively, for general accident ('arad 'amm) is not considered in definitions according to the later scholars, among them the author, and he will explicitly state that. Similarly, species (naw'), as understood from their usages, for they restricted the definiens to definition (hadd) and description (rasm) and did not consider in either of them species and general accident. Rather, they were mentioned previously only by way of digression and exhaustive treatment of the divisions of the universals. Some of the research commentators said: it could be said that the intention of the commentator (may God have mercy on him) from it is the five universals collectively, because species may be a part of the definiens, like the definition of a human being as 'such an animal', and general accident may also be a part of the definiens, as will come, God willing. And I say: this, although true in itself, is not compatible with attributing the remaining space to the author, so reflect. (Mirza Muhammad Ali)
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of a comment on the components of the definiens (المعرف). The author first states that the five universals are not all used in definitions according to later logicians: 'arad 'amm (general accident) and naw' (species) are excluded. Definitions are of two types: hadd (essential definition) and rasm (descriptive definition). The earlier mention of all five universals was just for completeness. Then a commentator objects that species can be part of a definiens (e.g., defining 'human' as a certain type of 'animal') and general accident can also be used. The author concedes this truth but says it does not fit the context of the original text (the phrase 'attributing the space' likely means that the original author's intention was not to include them). This shows a nuanced debate within the tradition about which universals are definitional components.

Key Terms

العرض العام

Checkpoint
According to the author of the passage, which two universals are NOT considered in definitions by later logicians?
A) Genus and species
B) Species and general accident
C) Differentia and property
D) Property and general accident

Key Takeaway
Later logicians restrict definitions to hadd and rasm, effectively excluding species and general accident from the definiens, though exceptions are debated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition of 'al-‘illa al-mu’aththira' (effective cause) in usul al-fiqh: 'a manifest, regular attribute that is suitable for legislation.' Identify the universals used: genus (attribute), differentia (manifest, regular, suitable). Why are species and general accident not needed here?
?
Give an example from hadd where species could be a part (like defining 'Rumi' as 'human of a certain type'). Then explain why later logicians still prefer to exclude species from the standard definitional framework.

Critique of the Definition of Mu'arraf and al-Sharif's Response
Author critiques a definition and presents al-Sharif's refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical problem in the famous definition of mu'arraf and explain how al-Sharif's concept of nazar resolves it.

Core Idea
The definiens does not cause conceptualization by logical entailment, but only when actively considered.

This lesson examines a critical refinement of the definition of 'mu'arraf' (definiendum). The author shows that the definition 'its conceptualization necessitates conceptualization of the thing defined' leads to circularity and fails for entailments. al-Sharif responds by restricting the necessitation to the context of intellectual consideration (nazar), preserving the utility of definitions without logical paradox. Understanding this refinement is key to evaluating definitions in Islamic logic and sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition under critique
Find the definition: 'its conceptualization necessitates conceptualization of this thing'. This is the famous definition of the definiendum (mu'arraf).
The definiendum is said to 'cause' conceptualization of the thing defined.
2
Extract the two counterexamples
First, entailments (multazimat): conceptualizing a clear concomitant of something does not mean the concomitant is a definiens. Second, the definiens itself: conceptualizing the definiens as such requires prior conceptualization of the definiendum, creating circularity.
These show the definition is too broad and circular.
3
Analyze the attempted defense and its failure
One might argue that 'summary conceptualization' does not necessitate 'detailed conceptualization'. But the author points out that even summary conceptualization of the definiendum requires detailed conceptualization of the definiens, so the defense fails.
The summary/detail distinction does not save the definition.
4
Understand al-Sharif's resolution
al-Sharif restricts the necessitation to 'bi-tariq al-nazar' (by way of consideration). That is, the definiens leads to conceptualization only when one actively considers it, not as a logical entailment.
This aligns with the purpose of logic: explaining how concepts are acquired.
5
Connect to the purpose of logic
The goal of the art (logic) is to explain the method of acquiring conceptualizations and assents. The redefined notion of necessitation fits this practical purpose.
Definitions are tools for the mind, not absolute logical principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) قوله ليفيد تصور هذا الشيء: هذا القيد لاخراج المحمول الذى لم يكن الغرض منه القادة التصور ثم انه عدل عن التعريف المشهور و هو يستلزم تصوره تصور هذا الشيء، لانتقاضه بالملزومات بالنسبة الى لوازمها البيئة و بالمعرف من حيث هو معرف فان تصوره من حيث هو كذلك اى المعرف يستلزم تصور معرفه لان تحقق تصوره من هذه الحيثية لا يكون الأبعد تصور معرفه، فظهر من ذلك ضعف ما يقال من ان استلزام تصور المعرف بالكسر ممنوع بان تصور الشيء مجملاً لا يستلزم تصوره مفصلاً. الضعف ان تصور المعرف مجملاً لا يكون الا بعد تصور معرفه مفصلاً فقد استلزم تصور المعرف و وجه من حيث انه كذلك تصور المعرف استلزام المعلول للملة وظهر ايضاً ضعف ما اورده المحقق الدواني من ان تصور ماهية المعرف قد يحصل بدون المعرف بالوجه السابق على الكسب. و اجاب المحقق الشريف عن الانتقاض : بان المراد من الاستلزام بطريق النظر بقرينة ما سبق من ان الموصل بالنظر الى التصور يسمى قولاً شارحاً وان المقصود من الفن بيان طريق اكتساب التصورات و التصديقات. (عبد الرحيم)
(2) His statement: 'to cause conceptualization of this thing': this restriction excludes the predicate whose purpose is not to benefit conceptualization. Then he altered the famous definition, which is 'its conceptualization necessitates conceptualization of this thing', because it is refuted by entailments (multazimat) with respect to their clear concomitants, and by the definiens (muʿarrif) insofar as it is a definiens. For its conceptualization insofar as it is such, i.e. the definiens, necessitates conceptualization of the definiendum, because the realization of its conceptualization from this perspective is not except after conceptualization of the definiendum. From that appears the weakness of what is said: that the necessitation of conceptualization of the definiendum is denied because conceptualization of a thing in summary does not necessitate its conceptualization in detail. The weakness: conceptualization of the definiendum in summary does not occur except after conceptualization of the definiens in detail. So the conceptualization of the definiendum in the aspect that it is such is a necessitation like the necessitation of the effect from the cause. Also appeared the weakness of what was objected by al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawani: that conceptualization of the essence of the definiendum may occur without the definiens in the manner prior to acquisition. And al-Muhaqqiq al-Sharif answered the refutation: that what is meant by 'necessitation' is by way of consideration (bi-tariq al-nazar) by the indication of what preceded: that what leads by consideration to conceptualization is called an explicative statement, and the purpose of the art is to explain the way of acquiring conceptualizations and assents. (Abd al-Rahim)
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the definition of 'mu'arraf' (definiendum). The author first notes that the phrase 'to cause conceptualization of this thing' excludes predicates that are not intended to produce conceptualization. Then he discusses the famous definition: 'its conceptualization necessitates conceptualization of this thing'. He points out two problems: (1) Entailments (multazimat): if you conceptualize an entailment, you also conceptualize the entailed, but that does not mean the entailment is a definiens. (2) The definiens itself: conceptualizing a definiens as such requires prior conceptualization of the definiendum, creating a circularity. Then he refutes a counterargument that summary conceptualization does not entail detailed conceptualization, showing that summary conceptualization of the definiendum itself requires detailed conceptualization of the definiens. He also refutes al-Dawani's objection that the essence of the definiendum can be known without a definiens. Finally, he reports al-Sharif's answer: the necessitation is by way of consideration (nazar), meaning that the definiens leads to conceptualization when considered, not that it is a logical entailment. This aligns with the purpose of logic: to explain how to acquire concepts.

Key Terms
المعرف بالكسر
المعرف بالفتح
الملزومات
النظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, al-Muhaqqiq al-Sharif's answer to the refutation of the definition is that the necessitation is by way of:
A) Logical entailment
B) Consideration (nazar)
C) Intuitive grasp
D) Divine illumination

Key Takeaway
A definition's ability to cause conceptualization is not absolute but depends on active intellectual consideration (nazar).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'The definiendum (mu'arraf) is that whose conceptualization necessitates conceptualization of the thing defined.' Using al-Sharif's response, explain how this definition can still be useful despite the apparent circularity.
?
In a fiqh text, a jurist says: 'The definition of fasād (invalidity in worship) is the occurrence of a defect that nullifies the act.' Apply the critique from this lesson: is this definition vulnerable to the same objections? How would you defend it?

Understanding Kunh and Complete Definition
Author defines 'kunh' and illustrates complete definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a complete definition (hadd tamm) and distinguish it from a mere description (rasm) in Islamic texts.

Core Idea
The complete definition reveals a thing's essence through its genus and differentia.

In logic, knowing the essence of something is the deepest form of conceptualization. This passage introduces 'kunh' as the essence and shows that only a complete definition—like 'rational animal' for human—conveys that essence fully. Understanding this distinction is key to evaluating definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find 'al-kunh' in the Arabic. Note its linguistic meaning (substance, limit, measure) and technical meaning (essence/reality of a thing composed of essential attributes).
The shift from linguistic to technical meaning is common in Islamic logic.
2
Extract the definition of 'kunh'
The passage defines 'kunh' as 'haqiqat al-shay' wa dhatiyyatihi' (the reality of a thing and its essential attributes). These essential attributes (dhatiyyat) are what constitute the quiddity.
3
Identify what gives knowledge of the essence
The author states that the conceptualization (tasawwur) that conveys the essence is the complete definition (al-hadd al-tamm). Example: 'al-hayawan al-natiq' for 'insan'.
The complete definition must include the proximate genus (hayawan) and differentia (natiq).
4
Distinguish complete definition from description
A complete definition (hadd tamm) gives the essence, while a description (rasm) gives only accidents or properties. This passage implies that only hadd tamm conveys kunh.
In later sections, the author contrasts hadd and rasm explicitly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳) الكنه بالضم فى اللغة جوهر الشيء و غايته و قدره و المراد به ههنا حقيقة الشيء وذاتياته التي ركب منها والتصور الذى افاد كنه الشيء و حقيقته هو الحد التام مثل: «الحيوان الناطق» في تعريف الانسان. (عبدالرحيم)
(3) 'Kunh' (with damm [on the kaf]) in language means the substance of a thing, its utmost limit, and its measure. What is meant by it here is the reality of a thing and its essential attributes (dhatiyyat) from which it is composed. And the conceptualization that conveys the kunh and reality of a thing is the complete definition (hadd tamm), like 'rational animal' in defining 'human'. (Abd al-Rahim)
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion of the term 'kunh' (essence). The author first gives the linguistic meaning: substance, utmost limit, measure. Then the technical meaning in logic: the reality of a thing and its essential constituents (dhatiyyat). The conceptualization that conveys this essence is the complete definition (hadd tamm), which includes the proximate genus and differentia. The example is 'rational animal' for 'human'. This clarifies that only a complete definition gives the essence, not a description (rasm).

Key Terms
الكنه
الحد التام
الذاتيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is an example of a complete definition (hadd tamm) that conveys the kunh?
A) 'Animal' for human
B) 'Rational animal' for human
C) 'Walking being' for human
D) 'Body' for human

Key Takeaway
The complete definition, consisting of proximate genus and differentia, alone conveys the essence (kunh) of a thing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Identify a complete definition in a fiqh text: Find the definition of 'riba' in al-Muwatta' or another fiqh manual. Write down the genus and differentia. Is it a hadd tamm or rasm?
?

Why the Definition of 'Mu'arraf' Includes 'Or by a Distinguishing Mark'
Author explains why 'or by a distinguishing mark' is added to the definition of 'mu'arraf'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the disjunctive phrase 'or by a distinguishing mark' is necessary in the definition of 'mu'arraf' to include incomplete definitions (hudud naqisa) and descriptions (rusum).

Core Idea
Definitions can be by essence or by distinction; logicians refined the definition to cover both.

In this lesson, we examine a key refinement in the definition of 'mu'arraf' (definiens) in Islamic logic. The standard definition was 'that whose conceptualization leads to conceptualization of the thing or to its distinctness from others.' Logicians added the second disjunct to ensure that incomplete definitions and descriptions are included. We will see why this addition was not redundant and how it resolves a potential dilemma.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two kinds of definitions
In the passage, the author distinguishes complete definitions (hadd tamm) which give the essence, from incomplete definitions (hadd naqis) and descriptions (rasm) which only give a distinguishing mark. Recognize that the latter do not reveal the essence but still serve as definitions.
2
Understand the potential problem
Without the addition of 'or by a distinguishing mark', the definition of 'mu'arraf' would either exclude these definitions (making it non-comprehensive) or be redundant if 'conceptualization' already implies distinction. The author addresses this imagined dilemma.
The problem is that if only essence-giving definitions count, many valid definitions are excluded; if 'conceptualization' alone covers both, the second disjunct is redundant.
3
See the solution
The author clarifies that 'conceptualization' in the definition is broader than the usual sense; it includes both conceptualization by essence and mere distinction. This resolves the dilemma because the addition explicitly includes definitions that only distinguish without giving essence.
Thus the definition is comprehensive: it covers both essential and non-essential definitions.
4
Analyze why 'or' is used
The conjunction 'or' indicates a genuine disjunction: the first branch aims at essence (even if it also distinguishes), the second aims only at distinction. This ensures no overlap and maintains logical precision.
The two types are mutually exclusive in intent, even if both lead to distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴) قوله او بوجه يمتاز عن جميع ما عداه هذا التعميم ليشتمل التعريف على الحدود الناقصه و الرسوم فانها لا تفيد تصور الشيء بالكنه بل امتيازه عن جميع ما عداه كما سيأتي . وفيه اشارة الى دفع ما ربما يتوهم من ان احد الامرين لازم هنا اما عدم كون هذا التعريف جامعاً او اشتمال تعريف القوم على مستدرك حيث قالوا: هو ما يستلزم تصوره تصور الشيء او اميتازه عن كل ما عداه كما هو ظاهر. و حاصله ان التصور هنا أعم منه في عبارة القوم فان مرادهم منه التصور بالكنه فلذا احتاجوا إلى زيادة قولهم أو امتيازه عن كل ما عداه فلا يلزم محذور، هذا. لا يقال: ان مايفيد تصوره تصور الشيء بالكنه يفيد تصوره بوجه يمتاز عن جميع الاغيار ايضاً فلا العطف بـ «او» المفيدة للتقابل و الايلزم ان يجعل قسيماً له. يصح لانا نقول: المراد او بوجه يمتاز عن جميع ما عداه من غير ان يفيد الاطلاع على الكنه فصار حاصل المعنى ان المعرف ما يفيد تصوره تصور الشيء اما بوجه يمتاز عن جميع ما عداه مع الاطلاع على الكنه أو بوجه يمتاز عن جميع ما عداه من غير ان يطلع على الكنه او نقول: المقصود بالذات في الشق الأول هو الاطلاع على الكنه و ان استلزم ذلك الامتياز عن جميع الاغيار لكنه غير مراد بخلافه في الشق الثاني فان المقصود فيه هو نفس الامتياز فقط فافهم. (میرزا محمد علی)
(4) His statement: 'or by a distinguishing mark from all others' – this generalization includes in the definition incomplete definitions (hudud naqisa) and descriptions (rusum), for they do not convey conceptualization of the thing by essence (kunh), but rather its distinctness from all others, as will come. In it is an indication to repel what might be imagined: that one of two things is necessary here: either this definition is not comprehensive, or the definition of the people includes a redundant element, where they said: 'it is that whose conceptualization necessitates conceptualization of the thing or its distinctness from all others' as is apparent. And the summary: that 'conceptualization' here is more general than it in the expression of the people, for what they mean by it is conceptualization by essence; therefore they needed to add their statement 'or its distinctness from all others', so no problematic consequence follows. It cannot be said: that what its conceptualization conveys conceptualization of the thing by essence also conveys its conceptualization in a manner distinct from all others, so the conjunction with 'or' that indicates opposition is not valid, and it would necessitate making it a counterpart of it. It is correct, for we say: what is meant is 'or by a distinguishing mark from all others' without conveying the knowledge of the essence. So the meaning becomes: the definiens is that whose conceptualization conveys conceptualization of the thing either by a distinguishing mark from all others with knowledge of the essence, or by a distinguishing mark from all others without gaining knowledge of the essence. Or we say: the intended by essence in the first branch is the knowledge of the essence, even if that entails distinction from all others, but it is not intended; unlike the second branch, for what is intended therein is the distinction itself. So understand. (Mirza Muhammad Ali)
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage expands on the definition of 'mu'arraf' by explaining the addition 'or by a distinguishing mark from all others'. The author says this addition is meant to include incomplete definitions and descriptions, which do not give the essence but only distinguish the thing. He then addresses a potential objection: without this addition, the definition would be either not comprehensive (if only essence-giving definitions count) or redundant (if 'conceptualization' already implies distinctness). The solution is that 'conceptualization' in this context is more general than the usual sense; it includes both conceptualization by essence and mere distinction. Then he clarifies why 'or' is used: the two disjuncts are genuinely different because the first aims at essence (even if it also distinguishes), while the second aims only at distinction. This shows the precision with which logicians framed the definition of definition.

Key Terms
الحد الناقص
الرسم
الامتياز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did logicians add 'or by a distinguishing mark' to the definition of 'mu'arraf'?
A) To exclude incomplete definitions
B) To include descriptions that do not give the essence
C) To make the definition more concise
D) To align with common usage

Key Takeaway
The definition of 'mu'arraf' is carefully crafted to include both essence-giving and distinguishing-only definitions, showing the precision of Islamic logicians in covering all valid definitions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'Man is a rational animal' (hadd tamm). Explain why this definition also provides a distinguishing mark, but the logicians still treat it under the first branch (essence-intending).
?

When Does the Specific Give the General?
Critical analysis of when the specific gives the general

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the claim 'conceptualizing the specific gives the general' by identifying the conditions (essential/accidental, mode of conceptualization) under which it holds or fails.

Core Idea
The specific never truly produces the general; it only reminds you of what you already know.

A common logical maxim states that knowing the more specific (al-akhass) gives knowledge of the more general (al-a'amm). But is that always true? In this dense passage from a supercommentary, the author dissects the claim by considering whether the general is essential or accidental to the specific, and whether the specific is known by essence or by description. He ultimately weakens the claim by pointing out the chronological priority of the general. This precision prevents sloppy definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim
The passage begins by noting that 'the specific under some aspect is the same as the general under some aspect.' This sets up the claim that conceptualizing the specific might automatically yield the general. Your task: locate where the author quotes or paraphrases this claim.
The claim is implicit: 'تصور الأخص يفيد تصور الأعم' – conceptualizing the specific benefits conceptualizing the general.
2
Distinguish essential vs. accidental general
The author uses two key terms: dhāti (essential, part of the quiddity) and ʿaraḍī (accidental, a property not in the quiddity). Identify which of these the general may be in each scenario.
E.g., 'animal' is essential to 'human', while 'walking' is accidental.
3
Determine the mode of conceptualization of the specific
The specific can be conceptualized 'by essence' (bil-kunh) – i.e., via its complete essential definition – or 'not by essence' (lā bil-kunh) – via description or incomplete definition. The passage lists several subtypes: complete description, incomplete definition, etc.
Example: 'human' conceptualized by essence is 'rational animal'; by description as 'walking, laughing'.
4
Walk through the four main cases
Combine the two variables: (a) essential general + specific by essence → claim holds. (b) accidental general + specific not by essence → claim may hold if definition includes general accident. (c) accidental general + specific by essence → claim fails. (d) essential general + specific by incomplete definition/description → claim fails (except some exceptions). List each case from the passage.
The passage also adds a special exception for complete description or certain incomplete definitions.
5
Analyze the final critique
The author ultimately says the claim is weak because conceptualization of the general must precede that of the specific. So the later specific cannot 'produce' the prior general. Unless we interpret it as 'the desire to conceptualize the specific necessitates conceptualization of the general' – a psychological, not logical, claim.
This is a key epistemological point: priority in knowledge order prevents the later from being the cause of the earlier.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵) انما فسر بذلك لان الاخص من وجه هو نفس الاعم من وجه و قد ذكر حاله آنفا (محمد علی) (ء) هذا اذا كان الاعم ذاتياً والاخص متصوراً بالكنه كالمثال الذي ذكره المحشى فله وجه في و هكذا اذا كان الاعم عرضياً والاخص متصوراً لا بالكنه ان جوز نا تركيب المعرف من العرض العام مع الفصل او الخاصة كما اذا تصورنا الانسان بانه ماش ضاحك او ناطق، فقد تصورنا في ضمنه الماشى باحد الوجهين واما اذا كان الاعم عرضياً والاخص متصوراً بالكنه فلا يفيد تصور الاخص تصور فانه لا يلزم من تصور الانسان بالحد التام تصور الماشى ايضاً كما هو ظاهر و كذا اذا كان الاعم ذاتياً وكان الاخص متصوراً بالحد الناقص البسيط و الرسم الناقص مطلقا واما اذا كان متصوراً بالرسم التام أو الحد الناقص المركب من الجنس البعيد والفصل القريب، فيجوز أيضاً ان يفيد تصوره تصور الاعم فتأمل . الأعم وبعد اللتيا واللتي فالقول بان تصور الاخص يفيد تصور الاعم لا يخلو عن ضعف، ضرورة تقدم تصور الاعم على تصور الاخص حفلا يصدق على تصور الاخص المتأخر في الحصول انه مفيد لتصور الاعم المتقدم فيه. اللهم الا ان يراد أن ارادة تصور الاخص يوجب تصور الاعم فافهم . (محمد على) (۷) قوله باحد الوجهين اما التصور بالكنه او بالوجه و المراد بالوجه الذي تصورت به الحيوان هيهنا هو التصور بالكنه لانك اذا تصورت الانسان بانه حيوان ناطق فقد تصورت الحيوان بانه جسم نامی
(5) He only interpreted it thus because the more specific under one aspect is the same as the more general under one aspect, and its state was mentioned recently. (Muhammad Ali) (ء) This [case] is when the more general is essential (dhati) and the more specific is conceptualized by essence (kunh), like the example mentioned by the commentator; thus it has a face. And likewise when the more general is accidental ('aradi) and the more specific is conceptualized not by essence, if we permit composition of the definiens from general accident with differentia or property, as if we conceptualize 'human' as 'walking, laughing, or rational'; then we have conceptualized within it 'walking' in one of the two ways. But if the more general is accidental and the more specific is conceptualized by essence, then conceptualization of the specific does not benefit conceptualization of the [general], for it does not follow from conceptualizing 'human' by complete definition to conceptualizing 'walking' as well, as is apparent. And likewise if the more general is essential and the more specific is conceptualized by incomplete simple definition or incomplete description absolutely. But if it is conceptualized by complete description or incomplete definition composed of distant genus and proximate differentia, then it is also possible that its conceptualization benefits conceptualization of the more general, so reflect. After all this, the statement that conceptualization of the specific benefits conceptualization of the general is not free from weakness, due to the necessity of the priority of conceptualization of the general over conceptualization of the specific; so it is not true of the later conceptualization of the specific that it is beneficial for the prior conceptualization of the general. Unless it is meant that the desire to conceptualize the specific necessitates conceptualization of the general, so understand. (Muhammad Ali) (7) His statement: 'in one of the two ways' – either conceptualization by essence or by distinguishing mark. And what is meant by 'the way' in which you conceptualized 'animal' here is conceptualization by essence, because if you conceptualize 'human' as 'rational animal', then you have conceptualized 'animal' as 'growing body'.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a nuanced epistemological discussion of when conceptualizing a more specific concept (al-akhass) yields conceptualization of a more general concept (al-a'amm). It begins by noting that the specific is 'the general under one aspect' (i.e., the specific includes the general). The commentator then lists several cases. (1) If the general is essential and the specific is known by essence, then conceptualizing the specific gives the general. (2) If the general is accidental and the specific is known not by essence, it may give the general if the definition combines general accident with differentia. (3) If the general is accidental and the specific is known by essence, then no. (4) If the general is essential and the specific is known by incomplete definition or incomplete description, then no. (5) If the specific is known by complete description or certain incomplete definitions, it may give the general. However, the final verdict is that this claim is weak because conceptualization of the general must precede conceptualization of the specific chronologically, so the specific cannot be said to 'produce' the general. The only way is if we mean that the desire to conceptualize the specific causes us to conceptualize the general. The final note (7) clarifies that 'one of the two ways' in a previous comment refers to conceptualization by essence, as in the example 'rational animal' where 'animal' is grasped as 'growing body' (essential conceptualization).

Two Kinds of Definiens: Complete Definition and Mere Description
Author defines kunn and explains the definition of mu'arraf covering both complete and incomplete definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish a complete definition (hadd tamm) from a mere description (rasm) by checking whether the definiens conveys the kunn (essence) or merely marks out the thing from everything else.

Core Idea
A definition can either reveal the essence (kunn) or simply label the thing – both are valid in Islamic logic.

In this passage from the Hashiya, the commentator clarifies the meaning of 'kunn' and then unpacks the definition of 'mu'arraf' (the definiens). The matn's definition uses an 'or' that might seem redundant at first. As we walk through the commentary, we'll see that this 'or' is crucial to cover both definitions that reveal the inner reality and those that only serve to distinguish the thing from everything else.

Guided Path
1
Understand 'kunn'
Kunn is the essence and essential attributes of a thing. The complete definition (hadd tamm) gives the kunn, e.g., 'rational animal' for man.
2
Identify the definition of 'mu'arraf'
The matn defines mu'arraf as 'that whose conception yields conception of the thing OR distinguishes it from everything else'.
3
Recognize two types of definiens
The disjunction covers: (a) definitions that give kunn (hadd tamm) and (b) definitions that only distinguish (incomplete definitions and descriptions).
4
Analyze the objection
One might think the definition is redundant (if something gives kunn, it also distinguishes) or non-comprehensive (if it distinguishes without giving kunn).
5
Understand the resolution
The commentator argues that 'conception' in the matn is broader than the earlier logicians' usage, which referred only to conception by kunn. Thus 'or' indicates two different intentions: one that gives essence (implicitly distinguishing) and one that only distinguishes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(3) الكنه بالضم في اللغة جوهر الشيء وغايته وقدره، والمراد به ههنا حقيقة الشيء وذاتياته التي ركب منها، والتصور الذي أفاد كنه الشيء وحقيقته هو الحد التام مثل: «الحيوان الناطق» في تعريف الإنسان. (4) قوله: أو بوجه يمتاز عن جميع ما عداه هذا التعميم ليشتمل التعريف على الحدود الناقصة والرسوم، فإنها لا تفيد تصور الشيء بالكنه بل امتيازه عن جميع ما عداه كما سيأتي. وفيه إشارة إلى دفع ما ربما يتوهم من أن أحد الأمرين لازم هنا، إما عدم كون هذا التعريف جامعاً أو اشتمال تعريف القوم على مستدرك حيث قالوا: هو ما يستلزم تصوره تصور الشيء أو امتيازه عن كل ما عداه كما هو ظاهر. وحاصله أن التصور هنا أعم منه في عبارة القوم، فإن مرادهم منه التصور بالكنه فلذا احتاجوا إلى زيادة قولهم: أو امتيازه عن كل ما عداه، فلا يلزم محذور. هذا. لا يقال: إن ما يفيد تصوره تصور الشيء بالكنه يفيد تصوره بوجه يمتاز عن جميع الأغيار أيضاً، فلا العطف بـ «أو» المفيدة للتقابل، وإلا لزم أن يجعل قسيماً له. لانا نقول: المراد أو بوجه يمتاز عن جميع ما عداه من غير أن يفيد الاطلاع على الكنه، فصار حاصل المعنى: أن المعرف ما يفيد تصوره تصور الشيء، إما بوجه يمتاز عن جميع ما عداه مع الاطلاع على الكنه، أو بوجه يمتاز عن جميع ما عداه من غير أن يطلع على الكنه. أو نقول: المقصود بالذات في الشق الأول هو الاطلاع على الكنه وإن استلزم ذلك الامتياز عن جميع الأغيار لكنه غير مراد، بخلافه في الشق الثاني فإن المقصود فيه هو نفس الامتياز فقط فافهم. (ميرزا محمد علي)
(3) Al-kunn with damm in language: the essence of a thing, its ultimate point, and its measure. What is meant here is the reality of a thing and its essential attributes from which it is composed. The conception that yields the kunn of a thing and its reality is the complete definition, such as 'rational animal' in the definition of man. (4) His saying: 'or by a way that distinguishes it from everything else' – this generalization is to include definitions [that are] incomplete descriptions and [true] descriptions, for they do not yield conception of the thing by its kunn, but rather its distinction from everything else, as will come. In it is an indication to refute what might be imagined: that one of two things is necessary here – either that this definition is not comprehensive, or that the definition of the people includes a superfluity, since they said: 'It is that whose conception necessitates the conception of the thing or its distinction from everything else', as is apparent. The gist: that 'conception' here is more general than in the expression of the people, for they mean by it conception by kunn, so they needed to add their saying 'or its distinction from everything else', so no problem arises. This. It cannot be said: that which yields conception of the thing by kunn also yields its conception in a way that distinguishes it from all others, so there is no conjunction with 'or' indicating opposition, otherwise it would become a coordinate with it. For we say: what is meant is 'or by a way that distinguishes it from everything else without yielding knowledge of the kunn'; so the meaning becomes: the definiens is that whose conception yields conception of the thing, either by a way that distinguishes it from everything else along with knowledge of the kunn, or by a way that distinguishes it from everything else without knowing the kunn. Or we say: the primary intention in the first part is knowledge of the kunn, even if that entails distinction from all others, but it is not intended; contrary to the second part, for the intention there is the distinction itself only. So understand. (Mirza Muhammad Ali)
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya defines two key terms: 'al-kunn' (the essence or inner reality of a thing) and 'al-mu'arraf' (the definiens). The commentator first clarifies that 'kunn' refers to the essential attributes of a thing, and the conception that conveys the kunn is the 'hadd tamm' (complete definition), exemplified by 'rational animal' for man. Then the passage expands on the definition of 'mu'arraf' given in the matn. The matn's definition says the mu'arraf is 'that whose conception yields conception of the thing or distinguishes it from everything else'. The commentator explains that this phrase is deliberately general to include not only complete definitions (hadd tamm) but also incomplete definitions (hudud naqisa) and descriptions (rusum). The objection that the definition might be redundant (since something that gives the essence also distinguishes) is answered: the word 'or' indicates two different types of definiens – one that gives essence (and thereby distinguishes implicitly) and one that only distinguishes without giving essence. The commentator offers two interpretations of the disjunction. All examples and discussions remain within the logical framework of Islamic mantiq, using the standard definition of man as rational animal.

Critiquing the Entailment of General from Specific in Mental Existence
Critique of entailment of general from specific in mental existence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the conditions under which the mental existence of a specific concept entails its general concept, as debated by al-Sharif and the author.

Core Idea
Mental existence does not automatically entail general from specific; it depends on how the specific is conceived.

In logic, it is often assumed that if something specific exists, its general category must also exist. However, this passage from a logic commentary reveals a crucial debate: does this hold in the mind as well? The commentator's objection and the author's refinement show that mental existence has its own rules. Understanding this will sharpen your ability to evaluate logical entailments in Islamic theological and legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original claim
Find the claim that the specific entails the general in mental existence because the specific has more conditions, making it rarer. The claim is from a commentary on the Risala.
The specific has more conditions, so if it exists, the general must also exist.
2
Locate al-Sharif's objection
Al-Sharif objects that entailment only holds if the general is essential to the specific and the specific is conceived by its kunn (essence). Why does he require these conditions?
He is concerned that if the general is accidental or the specific is only partially known, the entailment may not follow.
3
Understand the author's refinement
The author concedes al-Sharif's point but argues that even if the specific is not known by kunn but by a complete description (rasm tamm) or a composite incomplete definition (hadd naqis), entailment still holds. However, if the specific is known only by a simple incomplete definition (like genus alone), entailment fails.
This shows a nuanced view: the type of definition matters for whether the general is mentally present.
4
Apply the external vs mental distinction
Notice that al-Sharif also objects to the argument about conditions: in external existence, specific does entail general, but in mental existence, it may not. One can conceive a specific without its general, e.g., conceiving 'khamr' by its color without the concept 'intoxicant'.
This highlights the ontological difference between mental and external existence.
5
Test with an Islamic example
Consider the specific 'khamr' and the general 'intoxicant'. If a person only knows khamr as a red liquid, does mental existence of khamr entail mental existence of intoxicant? According to the passage, no, because the specific is not known by its essence or complete description.
This example from fiqh illustrates the practical import of the discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(8) قوله: لكن لما كان الأخص أقل وجوداً... قال بعض المحققين في شرح الرسالة: لأن وجود الخاص في العقل مستلزم لوجود العام، وربما يوجد العام في العقل بدون الخاص. واعترض عليه المحقق الشريف في حواشيه المعلقة عليه بأن هذا موقوف على أن يكون العام ذاتياً للخاص ويكون الخاص معقولاً بالكنه، وأما إذا لم يكن ذاتياً ولم يكن الخاص معقولاً بالكنه لم يلزم من وجوده في العقل وجود العام فيه. وأقول: هذا مسلم، ولكن الاستلزام على كون العام ذاتياً للخاص والخاص معقولاً بالكنه غير معقول، فإنه إذا كان العام ذاتياً والخاص غير معقول بالكنه بل بالرسم التام أو الحد الناقص إذا كان مركباً من الجنس البعيد والفصل القريب، صح ذلك الاستلزام أيضاً. لا يقال: يحتمل أن يكون مراده من كون الخاص معقولا بالكنه كونه معقولاً بالكنه في الجملة فيشمل الرسم التام والحد الناقص المذكور أيضاً. لأنا نقول: مع أن هذا خلاف اصطلاح القوم، يرد عليه أن يُسلم الاستلزام إذا كان الخاص معقولاً بالحد الناقص البسيط، وليس بصحيح البتة. وكذا إن قلنا بجواز تركيب الحد من العرض العام مع الفصل، ذلك الاستلزام وإن كان العام عرضياً غير ذاتي فافهم. ثم قال أيضاً في شرح الرسالة: وأو الخاصة، يصح أيضاً: شروط تحقق الخاص ومعانداته أكثر، فكل ما هو شرط ومعاند للعام فهو شرط ومعاند للخاص ولا ينعكس، وما يكون شروطه ومعانداته أكثر يكون وقوعه في العقل أقل، وما هو أقل في العقل فهو خفي عند العقل. واعترض عليه المحقق الشريف في حواشيه أيضاً بأن هذا بحسب الوجود الخارجي مسلم، فإنه كلما تحقق الخاص في الخارج تحقق العام فيه، وأما بحسب الوجود الذهني فلا، إذ جاز أن يعقل الخاص ولا يعقل العام كما مر آنفا، وأشار بذلك إلى ما نقلناه عنه فتأمل. (محمد علي)
(8) His saying: 'But since the specific has less existence...' Some investigators said in Sharh al-Risala: Because the existence of the specific in the mind entails the existence of the general, and sometimes the general exists in the mind without the specific. Al-Sharif objected in his glosses upon it: This depends on the general being essential to the specific and the specific being intelligible by kunn. But if it is not essential and the specific is not intelligible by kunn, its existence in the mind does not entail existence of the general therein. And I say: This is conceded, but the entailment on condition that the general is essential and the specific intelligible by kunn is not unintelligible; for if the general is essential and the specific is not intelligible by kunn but by a complete description or an incomplete definition composed of remote genus and proximate differentia, that entailment also holds. It cannot be said: It is possible that by 'the specific being intelligible by kunn' he means it is intelligible by kunn in a general sense, so that it includes the complete description and the mentioned incomplete definition. For we say: Apart from this being contrary to the terminology of the people, it would be conceded that the entailment holds if the specific is intelligible by a simple incomplete definition, but that is not correct at all. And likewise if we say it is permissible to compose the definition from a general accident with the differentia, that entailment would hold even if the general is accidental and non-essential; so understand. Then he also said in Sharh al-Risala: 'And the property (al-khassa) is also valid: the conditions of actualization of the specific and its opposites are more numerous, for every condition and opposite for the general is a condition and opposite for the specific, but not vice versa. And what has more conditions and opposites has less occurrence in the mind, and what is less in the mind is more obscure to the intellect.' Al-Sharif objected to this also in his glosses: This is conceded with respect to external existence, for whenever the specific is realized externally, the general is realized in it; but with respect to mental existence, no, for it is possible that the specific be conceived without the general, as mentioned earlier. He pointed to what we transmitted from him, so reflect. (Muhammad Ali)
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage critically examines a claim from a commentary on the Risala that the existence of the specific in the mind necessarily entails the existence of the general, because the specific has more conditions and thus is rarer. Al-Sharif (the commentator) objects that this entailment only holds if the general is essential to the specific and the specific is conceived by its kunn (essence). The author (Muhammad Ali) then refines: even if the specific is not conceived by kunn but by a complete description or a composite incomplete definition, it can still entail the general. However, if the specific is conceived by a simple incomplete definition (which does not give the full essence), then entailment fails. The discussion then shifts to the number of conditions: al-Sharif argues that while in external existence the specific implies the general, in mental existence it does not, as one can conceive a specific without its general (e.g., conceiving 'khamr' without conceiving 'intoxicant' if one only knows it by color). This shows the need to distinguish between mental and external existence. The example from fiqh: 'khamr' is specific, 'intoxicant' is general; in external reality, if khamr exists, intoxicant exists, but in the mind one might think of a red liquid without the property of intoxication.

الوجود الخارجي
معقول بالكنه

The entailment from specific to general in mental existence is not automatic; it depends on how the specific is conceived, distinguishing mental from external existence.

Resolving the Objection of Defining Mu'arraf by the Specific
Author presents an objection to the definition of mu'arraf and resolves it by distinguishing types of predication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish common predication from natural deviant predication and use this distinction to assess whether a definition is circular or definition by the specific.

Core Idea
Not all predication is equal: distinguishing common from deviant predication resolves apparent circularity in definitions.

This passage addresses a common objection in definition theory: if defining by the specific is invalid, then the definition of the most basic term 'mu'arraf' itself appears to fall into that trap. The key resolution lies in recognizing that the relation between the definiendum and definiens is one of coextensiveness under common predication, not specificity. By mastering this distinction, you will be able to defend definitions in logic and the Islamic sciences against charges of circularity.

Guided Path
1
Extract the objection
The objector claims that defining mu'arraf by 'ma yuqalu ala al-shay li-ifadati tasawwurihi' is definition by the specific, because not every mu'arraf is identical to that expression. This assumes the definiens is narrower in scope.
2
Analyze the meaning of 'specific'
The response clarifies that 'specific' must be understood under common predication (al-haml al-muta'araf), where one term is universally affirmative and the other is not. For example, 'every human is an animal' but 'some animal is not human'.
Under common predication, the predicate is broader than the subject.
3
Distinguish common from deviant predication
Common predication (haml muta'araf) involves a universal affirmative and a particular negative. Natural deviant predication (haml munharif tabi'i) is a non-standard relation where terms do not align by inclusion.
4
Test coextensiveness under common predication
Under common predication, every mu'arraf is a definition, and every definition is a mu'arraf. Thus the terms are convertible, not one more specific than the other. The negative proposition (that not every definition is that expression) is true only under deviant predication.
5
Conclude that no invalidity arises
Since under common predication the definiens and definiendum are coextensive, the definition is not by the specific. The objection rests on a misunderstanding of the predication type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: إذا لم يجز التعريف بالأخص كما هو مذهب المصنف، يلزم أن لا يصح تعريف المعرف، لأن ما يذكر في تعريف معرّف خاص فهو أخص من مطلق المعرف، إذ ليس كل معرف هو نفس ما يقال على الشيء لإفادة تصوره، فتعريفه به تعريف بالأخص.
قلنا: المراد بالأخص هنا أن يكون بحسب الحمل المتعارف، يعني أن صدق المعرف على جميع أفراد المعرف كما في الإنسان والحيوان، فإن كل إنسان حيوان وبعض الحيوان ليس بإنسان قضيتان متعارفتان، ومعرف المعرف ليس أخص بهذا المعنى، بل هما متساويان بطريق الحمل التعارفي، إذ كل فرد من المعرف يصدق عليه أنه ما يقال على الشيء لإفادة تصوره، وكذا كل فرد مما يقال على الشيء تصوره يصدق عليه أنه معرف. والسالبة المذكورة الصادقة هيهنا ليست بطريق الحمل المتعارف بل بطريق المنحرفة الطبيعية فافهم. هكذا أجاب المحقق الدواني. (شيخ عبد الرحيم)
If it is said: Since definition by the specific is not permissible, as is the doctrine of the author, it necessarily follows that the definition of 'mu'arraf' is not valid, because what is mentioned in the definition of a specific definiendum is more specific than absolute definiendum, since not every definiendum is identical to that which is said about a thing to convey its conception. Thus defining it by it is a definition by the specific. We say: What is meant by 'specific' here is that it is according to common predication, meaning that the predicate applies to all individuals of the subject, as in 'man' and 'animal', for 'every man is an animal' and 'some animal is not man' are two familiar propositions. But the definiendum of 'mu'arraf' is not specific in this sense; rather the two are coextensive under common predication, for every individual of the definiendum (mu'arraf) is true of it as being 'that which is said about a thing to convey its conception', and likewise every individual of that which is 'said about a thing to convey its conception' is true of it as being a mu'arraf. The true negative proposition mentioned here is not in the way of common predication but in the way of natural deviant predication; so understand. This is how al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawani answered. (Shaykh Abd al-Rahim)
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical objection against the definition of 'mu'arraf' (definiens). The objection states: if defining by the specific (akhass) is invalid, then the definition of 'mu'arraf' itself is invalid because the term used in that definition (namely 'ma yuqalu 'ala al-shay' li-ifadati tasawwurihi') is more specific than the absolute definiendum, since not every definiendum is identical to that expression. The answer clarifies that the 'specific' here must be understood according to common predication (haml muta'arif), where one term is predicated of the other in a universal affirmative but not vice versa. In the case of 'mu'arraf' and its definition, they are actually coextensive: every mu'arraf is a definition, and every definition is a mu'arraf. The negative proposition (that not every definition is that specific expression) is true only under 'natural deviant predication' (haml munharif tabi'i), not under common predication. Thus no invalidity arises. This exemplifies how logical precision distinguishes different modes of predication to avoid false objections. An example from usul al-fiqh: 'hukm' and 'taklif' are coextensive in some contexts but not in others.

Key Terms
الحمل المتعارف (al-haml al-muta'araf): Common or standard predication; a universal affirmative with a particular negative, so that the predicate is broader than the subject. [Note: Stable.]
الحمل المنحرف الطبيعي (al-haml al-munharif al-tabi'i): Natural deviant predication; a non-standard type of predication where the terms are not related by common inclusion, often used for logical analysis. [Note: This term is specific to later logical commentaries; earlier texts may not distinguish this explicitly.]
المعرف (al-mu'arraf): The definiendum; that which is being defined, i.e., the term or concept that the definiens explains. [Note: Stable.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, the objection that defining mu'arraf by 'ma yuqalu...' is definition by the specific is refuted by showing which of the following?
A) The definition is actually by the genus
B) The terms are coextensive under common predication
C) The specific is not a differentia
D) The definition uses a causal relation

Key Takeaway
The definition of 'mu'arraf' is not by the specific because under common predication the definiens and definiendum are convertible; the apparent specificity arises only under a non-standard mode of predication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'al-wajib is that which the Lawgiver demands in a binding manner.' Using the distinction between common and deviant predication, determine whether this definition suffers from the fallacy of definition by the specific.
?
In a class discussion, take the role of a mu'tarid objecting that the definition of 'mantiq' as 'a tool that protects against error in thinking' is definition by the specific. Then respond as a mujib using the concept of common predication to show coextensiveness.

The Four Relations between Definition and Defined
Author enumerates four types of relations and establishes equality as necessary for sound definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four possible relations between a definition and its definiendum, and determine whether a given definition satisfies ittirād and in'ikās.

Core Idea
A sound definition must be exactly equal in scope to what it defines.

In logic, a definition (had) must neither be too broad nor too narrow relative to the thing defined. The author of this passage, a commentator on classical logic, enumerates four possible relations between a definer (had) and the defined (mahdud) and argues that only equality (musawāt) is acceptable. He then formalizes this equality as two conditions: ittirād (the definition excludes non-instances) and in'ikās (the definition includes all instances). Understanding these conditions is crucial for evaluating definitions in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
List the four logical relations
Enumerate the four types: equivalence (musāwāt), complete difference (tabāyun), absolute generality/specificity (umūm wa khuṣūṣ muṭlaq), and generality/specificity in one respect (umūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh).
These are the only possible relations between two non-identical concepts.
2
Eliminate the impermissible types
The third and fourth types are ruled out because a definition must be coextensive with the defined; the second is ruled out because a definition must be predicable of the defined.
Predicability requires that the definition can be truly affirmed of every instance of the defined.
3
Establish equality as necessary
Only equality remains. This means the definition and the defined apply to exactly the same set of individuals.
Equality is expressed by two universal affirmative propositions.
4
Formulate the conditions of ittirād and in'ikās
Ittirād: every instance of the definition is an instance of the defined (the definition does not include aliens). In'ikās: every instance of the defined is an instance of the definition (the definition covers all members).
These correspond to the definition being a barrier (man') and comprehensive (jam').
5
Test a sample definition
Apply the conditions to a definition from Islamic science, e.g., 'Human is a rational animal'. Check ittirād: every rational animal is human? In classical ontology, yes. Check in'ikās: every human is rational animal? Yes. Therefore the definition is sound.
If either condition fails, the definition is either too broad or too narrow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم ان الشقوق العقلية بين المعرف والمحدود بعد ما لم يكن عينه لئلا يلزم ان يكون الشيء معلوماً قبل العلم به متصورة باربعة انواع: الاول ان يكونا متساويين والثاني ان يكونا متباينين. والثالث: ان يكونا اعم واخص مطلقاً. والرابع: ان يكونا اعم واخص من وجه. وقد تقرر في ما سبق عدم جواز الاخيرين وعلم من تعريفه بـ "ما يقال عليه" عدم جواز الثاني ايضاً لان مباين الشيء لا يحمل عليه فتعين الأول. وهذا معنى قوله فتعين ان يكون مساوياً له. وقد عرفت فيما ان المساواة راجعة الى موجبتين كليتين فلابد في صحة التعريف من صدق قضيتين موجبتين كليتين: احديهما: صدق المحدود على جميع مصاديق الحد وحمله عليه كلياً. و ثانيتهما عكسه اعني صدق الحد على جميع مصاديق المحدود و حمله عليه كلياً. ومن ذلك ما اصطلحوا عليه من أنهم يعبرون عن كون الحد مانعاً عن الاغيار بالاطراد كما يعبرون بالمنع وعن كونه جامعاً لافراد المحدود بالانعكاس كما يعبرون بالجمع و ذلك لاطراد صدق المحدود على مصاديق الحد على الاول و بالعكس على الثاني. فالمراد بالاطراد ان لا يكون شيء من مصاديق الحد الا و يصدق عليه المحدود و بالانعكاس ان لا يكون شيء من مصاديق المحدود الا و يصدق عليه الحد.
Know that the mental divisions between the definer and the defined, after it is not the same thing lest it necessitate that the thing be known before knowledge of it, are conceptually of four types: first, they are equal; second, they are completely different; third, one is absolutely more general and the other more specific; fourth, one is more general in one respect and more specific in another. It has been established in the preceding that the last two are not permissible, and from its definition as 'that which is predicated of a thing' it is known that the second is also impermissible because a thing completely different from another is not predicated of it. Thus the first is determined. This is the meaning of his statement: 'so it is determined that it be equal to it.' And you have known that equality reduces to two universal affirmative propositions. Therefore for the soundness of definition there must be two universal affirmative propositions true: one: the truth of the defined concerning all instances of the limit and its predication over them universally; and second, its converse, i.e., the truth of the limit concerning all instances of the defined and its predication over them universally. From this is what they have agreed upon: that they express the limit being a barrier against others by 'mutarid' as they express by 'man' (prevention), and its being comprehensive of the individuals of the defined by 'mun'akis' as they express by 'jam'' (inclusion). That is because of the constant (itarad) truth of the defined concerning instances of the limit in the first case, and the converse in the second. So by 'mutarid' is meant that there is no instance of the limit except that the defined is true of it; and by 'mun'akis' is meant that there is no instance of the defined except that the limit is true of it.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage explains the necessary relationship between a definition (had) and what it defines (mahdud). The author begins by listing four possible logical relations between two concepts when they are not identical (to avoid circularity): (1) equality (musawāt), (2) complete difference (tabāyun), (3) one is absolutely more general and the other more specific (umūm wa khuṣūṣ muṭlaq), and (4) each is more general in one respect and more specific in another (umūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh). The author then notes that the third and fourth have already been shown invalid (in earlier discussions), and the second is invalid because a definition must be predicable (maḥmūl) of the defined, which is impossible if they are completely different. Therefore, only equality (musawāt) remains. This equality means that the definition and the defined are coextensive: every instance of the definition is an instance of the defined, and vice versa. He then formalizes this as two universal affirmative propositions (qadiyyatān mūjibatān kulliyyatān): (a) the defined is true of all instances of the definition, and (b) the definition is true of all instances of the defined. The technical terms for these two conditions are 'al-ittirād' (the definition excludes all non-instances of the defined) and 'al-in'ikās' (the definition includes all instances of the defined). For example, in defining 'human' as 'rational animal', we require that every rational animal is human (ittirād) and every human is a rational animal (in'ikās). The author clarifies that 'ittirād' corresponds to the definition preventing entry of alien things (man'), and 'in'ikās' corresponds to its comprehensiveness (jam'). Thus, a sound definition must meet both conditions of coextension.

Key Terms
المعرف
الحد
المساواة
الاطراد
الانعكاس

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The definition and the defined are completely different (mutabāyinān).
C) The definition and the defined are equal (musāwiyān) in extension.
D) The definition is more general in one respect and more specific in another.

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must be coextensive with the defined, satisfying ittirād (exclusion of non-instances) and in'ikās (inclusion of all instances).
